Task instruction sent to agent 
# Kafka Connect REST API v1 to v2 Migration

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Kafka Connect REST API: the v1 connector resource handlers, the v2 connector resource handlers, and the version routing logic. Identify what changed between v1 and v2 in the task status and error response schemas.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

   151→    public final Connector createConnector(String listener, boolean isAdmin) {
   152→        Matcher listenerMatcher = LISTENER_PATTERN.matcher(listener);
   153→
   154→        if (!listenerMatcher.matches())
   155→            throw new ConfigException("Listener doesn't have the right format (protocol://hostname:port).");
   156→
   157→        String protocol = listenerMatcher.group(1).toLowerCase(Locale.ENGLISH);
   158→
   159→        if (!PROTOCOL_HTTP.equals(protocol) && !PROTOCOL_HTTPS.equals(protocol))
   160→            throw new ConfigException(String.format("Listener protocol must be either \"%s\" or \"%s\".", PROTOCOL_HTTP, PROTOCOL_HTTPS));
   161→
   162→        String hostname = listenerMatcher.group(2);
   163→        int port = Integer.parseInt(listenerMatcher.group(3));
   164→
   165→        ServerConnector connector;
   166→
   167→        if (PROTOCOL_HTTPS.equals(protocol)) {
   168→            SslContextFactory.Server ssl;
   169→            if (isAdmin) {
   170→                ssl = SSLUtils.createServerSideSslContextFactory(config, RestServerConfig.ADMIN_LISTENERS_HTTPS_CONFIGS_PREFIX);
   171→            } else {
   172→                ssl = SSLUtils.createServerSideSslContextFactory(config);
   173→            }
   174→            connector = new ServerConnector(jettyServer, ssl);
   175→            if (!isAdmin) {
   176→                connector.setName(String.format("%s_%s%d", PROTOCOL_HTTPS, hostname, port));
   177→            }
   178→        } else {
   179→            connector = new ServerConnector(jettyServer);
   180→            if (!isAdmin) {
   181→                connector.setName(String.format("%s_%s%d", PROTOCOL_HTTP, hostname, port));
   182→            }
   183→        }

   200→    public void initializeServer() {
   201→        log.info("Initializing REST server");
   202→
   203→        Slf4jRequestLogWriter slf4jRequestLogWriter = new Slf4jRequestLogWriter();
   204→        slf4jRequestLogWriter.setLoggerName(RestServer.class.getCanonicalName());
   205→        CustomRequestLog requestLog = new CustomRequestLog(slf4jRequestLogWriter, CustomRequestLog.EXTENDED_NCSA_FORMAT + " %{ms}T");
   206→        jettyServer.setRequestLog(requestLog);
   207→
   208→        /* Needed for graceful shutdown as per `setStopTimeout` documentation */
   209→        StatisticsHandler statsHandler = new StatisticsHandler();
   210→        statsHandler.setHandler(handlers);
   211→        jettyServer.setHandler(statsHandler);
   212→        jettyServer.setStopTimeout(GRACEFUL_SHUTDOWN_TIMEOUT_MS);
   213→        jettyServer.setStopAtShutdown(true);
   214→
   215→        try {
   216→            jettyServer.start();
   217→        } catch (Exception e) {
   218→            throw new ConnectException("Unable to initialize REST server", e);
   219→        }
   220→
   221→        log.info("REST server listening at {}, advertising URL {}", jettyServer.getURI(), advertisedUrl());
   222→        URI adminUrl = adminUrl();
   223→        if (adminUrl != null)
   224→            log.info("REST admin endpoints at {}", adminUrl);
   225→    }

    private byte[] serializeTargetState(TargetState state) {
        Struct connectTargetState = new Struct(TARGET_STATE_V1);
        // Older workers don't support the STOPPED state; fall back on PAUSED
        connectTargetState.put("state", state == STOPPED ? PAUSED.name() : state.name());
        connectTargetState.put("state.v2", state.name());
        return converter.fromConnectData(topic, TARGET_STATE_V1, connectTargetState);
    }

## Summary of Kafka Connect REST API Version-Related Files and Patterns

Based on my thorough exploration of the Kafka Connect codebase, I've identified the following REST API version-related files, patterns, and architectural elements:

### 1. **REST Resource Handlers and Endpoints**

**Location**: `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`

Key resource files:
- **ConnectorsResource.java** - Main REST resource at `@Path("/connectors")` handling connector CRUD operations
- **RootResource.java** - Root API endpoint at `@Path("/")` providing server info
- **ConnectorPluginsResource.java** - Plugin validation at `@Path("/connector-plugins")`
- **InternalConnectResource.java** - Internal cluster communication at `@Path("/connectors")`
- **InternalClusterResource.java** - Base class for internal endpoints (task configs, fence operations)
- **LoggingResource.java** - Admin endpoint for logging control

**Note**: There are **NO separate v1/v2 versioned resource paths** in the current implementation. All endpoints use the same paths across versions.

### 2. **ConnectorStateInfo and TaskStatus Response Handling**

**File**: `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/ConnectorStateInfo.java`

Key classes:
- **ConnectorStateInfo** - Container for connector and task state
  - Contains `ConnectorState` (nested class)
  - Contains `List<TaskState>` (nested class implementing Comparable)
- **AbstractState** - Base class with fields:
  - `state` (String) - Current state
  - `workerId` (String) - Worker ID
  - `trace` (String) - Error trace (non-empty only on failure)
  - `version` (String) - Plugin versio

247-assistanttext-
My comprehensive analysis is complete. I've thoroughly searched the Apache Kafka Connect codebase and documented all relevant files related to the REST API implementation. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**There are NO separate v1/v2 resource handlers** in the Kafka Connect REST API. Instead, the implementation uses:

1. **Single Unified API**: All REST endpoints are served by a single set of resource classes (ConnectorsResource, RootResource, etc.) without version-specific variants.

2. **Backward-Compatible Schema Evolution**: 
   - Response schemas use optional fields marked with `@JsonInclude` annotations
   - Old clients safely ignore new fields
   - New clients can handle older responses missing new fields

3. **Storage-Level Versioning**: The only explicit versioning found is in `KafkaConfigBackingStore` with:
   - `TARGET_STATE_V0`: Legacy schema
   - `TARGET_STATE_V1`: Enhanced schema with optional `state.v2` field
   - This dual-field approach maintains compatibility with old workers

4. **Error Response Consistency**: All endpoints return errors in the same `ErrorMessage` format with `error_code` and `message` fields.

5. **Task Status Schema**: Returned via `ConnectorStateInfo` containing state, worker_id, trace, and version fields for both connectors and tasks.

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all identified files, symbols, and a detailed explanation of the REST API architecture and versioning strategy.

Analysis\\n\\nThe Apache Kafka Connect implementation uses a **unified REST API without explicit v1/v2 path-based versioning**. The API versioning strategy relies on backward-compatible schema evolution rather than separate endpoint versions.\\n\\n### REST API Resource Handlers\\n\\n**Main Connector Resource Handler** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/ConnectorsResource.java):\\n- Primary handler for all connector-related REST operations\\n- Registered at @Path(\\\"/connectors\\\") with single implementation serving all API consumers\\n- Handles connector CRUD operations, status queries, task management, and restart operations\\n- Methods: listConnectors, createConnector, getConnector, getConnectorConfig, getConnectorStatus, getConnectorActiveTopics, resetConnectorActiveTopics, putConnectorConfig, patchConnectorConfig, restartConnector, stopConnector, pauseConnector, resumeConnector, getTaskConfigs, getTaskStatus, restartTask, destroyConnector, getOffsets, alterConnectorOffsets, resetConnectorOffsets\\n\\n**Internal Cluster Resource** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/InternalConnectResource.java and InternalClusterResource.java):\\n- Separate handler for inter-worker communication at @Path(\\\"/connectors\\\")\\n- Handles internal-only operations: putTaskConfigs (POST /{connector}/tasks) and fenceZombies (PUT /{connector}/fence)\\n- Used for cluster-internal communication, not exposed to external clients\\n\\n### API Version Strategy: Schema Evolution Instead of Path Versioning\\n\\n**No Separate v1/v2 Endpoints**: The codebase does not implement separate /v1/connectors or /v2/connectors paths. Instead, versioning is handled through:\\n\\n1. **Response Schema Backward Compatibility**:\\n   - ConnectorStateInfo.AbstractState includes: state (string), worker_id (string), trace (string, non-empty only on errors), version (string from plugin)\\n   - TaskState.TaskState extends AbstractState and adds: id (int)\\n   - Error responses use consistent ErrorMessage format: {error_code: int, message: string}\\n   - Optional fields are marked with @JsonInclude(JsonInclude.Include.NON_EMPTY) or custom filters, allowing old clients to ignore new fields\\n\\n2. **Storage Layer Versioning** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/KafkaConfigBackingStore.java):\\n   - TARGET_STATE_V0: Original schema with single \\\"state\\\" field (for backward compatibility with connectors written before STOPPED state existed)\\n   - TARGET_STATE_V1: Enhanced schema adding optional \\\"state.v2\\\" field (contains actual state: STOPPED)\\n   - Dual-field approach: Both \\\"state\\\" (PAUSED for stopped connectors) and \\\"state.v2\\\" (actual STOPPED) are written to satisfy old and new workers\\n   - During deserialization: reads \\\"state.v2\\\" if available, falls back to \\\"state\\\" for older records\\n   - This strategy allows mixed-version clusters where old workers don't support STOPPED state\\n\\n### Status Response Schemas\\n\\n**Task Status Response** (returned by getTaskStatus endpoint):\\n- ConnectorStateInfo containing:\\n  - name: String\\n  - connector: ConnectorState (state, worker_id, trace, version)\\n  - tasks: List<TaskState> where each TaskState has (id, state, worker_id, trace, version)\\n  - type: ConnectorType enum\\n- State enum values: UNASSIGNED, RUNNING, PAUSED, FAILED, DESTROYED, RESTARTING, STOPPED\\n- STOPPED state added later for connectors only (never for tasks)\\n\\n**Connector Status Response** (returned by getConnectorStatus endpoint):\\n- Same ConnectorStateInfo structure but typically used for connector-level status\\n- Includes all tasks associated with the connector\\n\\n**Error Response Schema**:\\n- Consistent across all endpoints: {\\\"error_code\\\": int, \\\"message\\\": String}\\n- Mapped by ConnectExceptionMapper from exceptions: ConnectRestException, NotFoundException, AlreadyExistsException, WebApplicationException\\n- HTTP status code + error_code both present in response\\n\\n### Version Routing Logic\\n\\nNo explicit version routing exists in the codebase. Instead:\\n\\n1. **Single Registration** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/ConnectRestServer.java):\\n   - ConnectRestServer extends RestServer and registers resources once\\n   - regularResources(): returns Arrays.asList(RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource)\\n   - adminResources(): returns Collections.singletonList(LoggingResource)\\n   - No variant resources for different API versions\\n\\n2. **REST Server Setup** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/RestServer.java):\\n   - Uses Jersey (jakarta.ws.rs) and Jetty (embedded HTTP server)\\n   - JacksonJsonProvider for JSON serialization/deserialization\\n   - ConnectExceptionMapper handles all exception-to-response conversions\\n   - No Accept-Version, X-API-Version, or similar headers are processed for routing\\n\\n3. **Configuration** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/RestServerConfig.java):\\n   - No API version configuration properties\\n   - Listeners configured via HTTP/HTTPS URIs without version specifiers\\n\\n### Key Findings\\n\\n**Versioning Approach**: Kafka Connect uses **transparent backward compatibility** rather than explicit API versioning:\\n- All clients use same endpoints regardless of Connect/client version\\n- New optional fields in responses are safely ignored by older clients\\n- Storage layer maintains dual representations for incompatible state transitions (e.g., STOPPED state addition)\\n- Plugin versions are included in responses (version field in task/connector states) but are informational only\\n\\n**No v1/v2 Split**: Despite the task's reference to v1 and v2 handlers, the actual implementation maintains a single unified API that evolves through optional field addition and storage-layer compatibility strategies. This is a common pattern for HTTP APIs serving diverse clients with varying versions.\\n\\n**Response Type Information**: Version information in responses comes from plugin implementations (ConnectorState.version, TaskState.version) and Kafka Connect version (ServerInfo.version), not from API versioning.\\n\"\n}\n",

Analysis\\n\\nThe Apache Kafka Connect implementation uses a **unified REST API without explicit v1/v2 path-based versioning**. The API versioning strategy relies on backward-compatible schema evolution rather than separate endpoint versions.\\n\\n### REST API Resource Handlers\\n\\n**Main Connector Resource Handler** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/ConnectorsResource.java):\\n- Primary handler for all connector-related REST operations\\n- Registered at @Path(\\\"/connectors\\\") with single implementation serving all API consumers\\n- Handles connector CRUD operations, status queries, task management, and restart operations\\n- Methods: listConnectors, createConnector, getConnector, getConnectorConfig, getConnectorStatus, getConnectorActiveTopics, resetConnectorActiveTopics, putConnectorConfig, patchConnectorConfig, restartConnector, stopConnector, pauseConnector, resumeConnector, getTaskConfigs, getTaskStatus, restartTask, destroyConnector, getOffsets, alterConnectorOffsets, resetConnectorOffsets\\n\\n**Internal Cluster Resource** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/InternalConnectResource.java and InternalClusterResource.java):\\n- Separate handler for inter-worker communication at @Path(\\\"/connectors\\\")\\n- Handles internal-only operations: putTaskConfigs (POST /{connector}/tasks) and fenceZombies (PUT /{connector}/fence)\\n- Used for cluster-internal communication, not exposed to external clients\\n\\n### API Version Strategy: Schema Evolution Instead of Path Versioning\\n\\n**No Separate v1/v2 Endpoints**: The codebase does not implement separate /v1/connectors or /v2/connectors paths. Instead, versioning is handled through:\\n\\n1. **Response Schema Backward Compatibility**:\\n   - ConnectorStateInfo.AbstractState includes: state (string), worker_id (string), trace (string, non-empty only on errors), version (string from plugin)\\n   - TaskState.TaskState extends AbstractState and adds: id (int)\\n   - Error responses use consistent ErrorMessage format: {error_code: int, message: string}\\n   - Optional fields are marked with @JsonInclude(JsonInclude.Include.NON_EMPTY) or custom filters, allowing old clients to ignore new fields\\n\\n2. **Storage Layer Versioning** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/KafkaConfigBackingStore.java):\\n   - TARGET_STATE_V0: Original schema with single \\\"state\\\" field (for backward compatibility with connectors written before STOPPED state existed)\\n   - TARGET_STATE_V1: Enhanced schema adding optional \\\"state.v2\\\" field (contains actual state: STOPPED)\\n   - Dual-field approach: Both \\\"state\\\" (PAUSED for stopped connectors) and \\\"state.v2\\\" (actual STOPPED) are written to satisfy old and new workers\\n   - During deserialization: reads \\\"state.v2\\\" if available, falls back to \\\"state\\\" for older records\\n   - This strategy allows mixed-version clusters where old workers don't support STOPPED state\\n\\n### Status Response Schemas\\n\\n**Task Status Response** (returned by getTaskStatus endpoint):\\n- ConnectorStateInfo containing:\\n  - name: String\\n  - connector: ConnectorState (state, worker_id, trace, version)\\n  - tasks: List<TaskState> where each TaskState has (id, state, worker_id, trace, version)\\n  - type: ConnectorType enum\\n- State enum values: UNASSIGNED, RUNNING, PAUSED, FAILED, DESTROYED, RESTARTING, STOPPED\\n- STOPPED state added later for connectors only (never for tasks)\\n\\n**Connector Status Response** (returned by getConnectorStatus endpoint):\\n- Same ConnectorStateInfo structure but typically used for connector-level status\\n- Includes all tasks associated with the connector\\n\\n**Error Response Schema**:\\n- Consistent across all endpoints: {\\\"error_code\\\": int, \\\"message\\\": String}\\n- Mapped by ConnectExceptionMapper from exceptions: ConnectRestException, NotFoundException, AlreadyExistsException, WebApplicationException\\n- HTTP status code + error_code both present in response\\n\\n### Version Routing Logic\\n\\nNo explicit version routing exists in the codebase. Instead:\\n\\n1. **Single Registration** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/ConnectRestServer.java):\\n   - ConnectRestServer extends RestServer and registers resources once\\n   - regularResources(): returns Arrays.asList(RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource)\\n   - adminResources(): returns Collections.singletonList(LoggingResource)\\n   - No variant resources for different API versions\\n\\n2. **REST Server Setup** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/RestServer.java):\\n   - Uses Jersey (jakarta.ws.rs) and Jetty (embedded HTTP server)\\n   - JacksonJsonProvider for JSON serialization/deserialization\\n   - ConnectExceptionMapper handles all exception-to-response conversions\\n   - No Accept-Version, X-API-Version, or similar headers are processed for routing\\n\\n3. **Configuration** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/RestServerConfig.java):\\n   - No API version configuration properties\\n   - Listeners configured via HTTP/HTTPS URIs without version specifiers\\n\\n### Key Findings\\n\\n**Versioning Approach**: Kafka Connect uses **transparent backward compatibility** rather than explicit API versioning:\\n- All clients use same endpoints regardless of Connect/client version\\n- New optional fields in responses are safely ignored by older clients\\n- Storage layer maintains dual representations for incompatible state transitions (e.g., STOPPED state addition)\\n- Plugin versions are included in responses (version field in task/connector states) but are informational only\\n\\n**No v1/v2 Split**: Despite the task's reference to v1 and v2 handlers, the actual implementation maintains a single unified API that evolves through optional field addition and storage-layer compatibility strategies. This is a common pattern for HTTP APIs serving diverse clients with varying versions.\\n\\n**Response Type Information**: Version information in responses comes from plugin implementations (ConnectorState.version, TaskState.version) and Kafka Connect version (ServerInfo.version), not from API versioning.\\n\"\n}\n",
